Text File : app_tutorial
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
Battle Passes
A new Battle Pass will be available each season.\nBy increasing the level of your Battle Pass, you’ll\nbe able to earn various rewards.
You can raise the level of a Battle Pass by taking part in\nRanked Battles and competitions to obtain Season Points.
Some rewards are only available by purchasing a Premium\nBattle Pass. The Premium Battle Pass can be purchased from\nthe Shop screen.
The Shop Screen
The Shop screen is divided into two sections:\nthe Premium Shop and the Frontier Shop.
In the Premium Shop, you can purchase memberships,\nPremium Battle Passes, and more.
In the Frontier Shop, you can exchange your VP for\nthings like held items for your Pokémon or new clothes.
Cordy’s Missions
With Cordy’s missions, you can earn and claim rewards by\nfulfilling certain conditions. Some missions are updated on a\ndaily basis, while others are newly assigned each week.
Achievements
Here you can view various achievements you might set your\nsights on completing. Meet their conditions and you’ll receive\nrewards including badges, titles, and more!
Online Competitions
Online Competitions allow you to battle other Trainers\naround the world by connecting to the internet.
Enter a competition, and you’ll be able to battle your fellow\ncompetitors for the length of the event. Some competitions\nalso offer special rewards. But note that if you ever need to\nwithdraw from a competition, you must do so before it begins!
Battle Data
With the Battle Data feature, you can check the results\nof various competitions and Ranked Battles seasons.\nYou can also see data about the Pokémon that were\nmost frequently used in battles.
The Style Screen
In this area, you can change your clothing,\nyour hair and cosmetics, the pose you strike\nwhen entering battle, and more.
Put together a combination that’s all your own,\nthen save it as a preset style!
Trainer Profiles
On the Profile screen, you can check a Trainer’s details, such as\ntheir Trainer ID. When viewing your own profile, you can also\nchange up your badges, Trainer icon, and title.
You can choose who can see your profile\nin the Settings menu.
Private Battles
Private Battles are held by creating rooms, in which you face\noff against friends and other Trainers under various battle rules.
Others can join a room you’ve made by inputting its Room ID.\nYou can also send invitations to friends, which will allow them\nto join a room directly without needing to know the ID.
If you’d rather spectate than battle, you can choose to watch\nPrivate Battles taking place between other Trainers in the room.
Stats & More
On this screen you can see a summary of information about a\nPokémon and also set its battle name, title, and more.
Recruiting Pokémon
You can [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]recruit[System:Color a="255" ] Pokémon from the available\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]rosters[System:Color a="255" ] you’ll find at Roster Ranch.
Every 22 hours, you’ll be able to meet a new lineup of\nPokémon to recruit from—without using VP! You can\nshorten this waiting time using VP or Quick Coupons.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Note: The lineup of Pokémon you can meet\nduring the tutorial is fixed and will not change.[System:Color a="255" ]
Let’s get to recruitin’, shall we?
Go on, now, don’t be shy! Pick out a Pokémon\nthat strikes your fancy.\c\nAnd don’t forget—it’d usually cost you VP to go\nrecruitin’ a Pokémon permanently.\c\nBut just this once, I’ll let you pick for nothin’!
Training Pokémon
By using VP, you can train Pokémon to change their\nstat points, stat alignments, moves, Abilities, and more.
Replica Teams
With the Replica Team feature, you can make new\nBattle Teams based on the teams that other Trainers\nhave shared. You can share your own teams, too!
If your Pokémon have different stats, moves, or Abilities\nthan those on the Battle Team you’re replicating, you can\ntrain all your Pokémon at once to make them match.
Collecting Pokémon from Pokémon HOME
Pokémon that you send from Pokémon HOME to\nvisit here in Pokémon Champions can be collected\nfrom Roster Ranch.
These visiting Pokémon may have their stats or Abilities\nchanged to help them be better suited to battle here.
Their moves won’t be changed automatically, but you can\nalways change them yourself by training your Pokémon.\nThis lets you replace any moves that can’t be used here\nin Pokémon Champions.
Sending Pokémon Back to Pokémon HOME
Pokémon you’ve brought over to visit from Pokémon HOME\ncan be sent back to Pokémon HOME at any time.
Training done here won’t carry over to Pokémon HOME, but if\nthe same Pokémon visit Pokémon Champions again, any training\nthey received here will be saved as long as those Pokémon are\nstill in the same form as when they last visited.
Your Pokémon Box
In your Box, you can view the Pokémon you’ve\nrecruited and make yourself some Battle Teams.
Use the sorting and filtering functions, or choose\nto label or favorite certain Pokémon, to make them\neasy to find whenever you want.
To battle other Trainers, you’ll need to make a\nBattle Team with six Pokémon on it, zzt-zzt!\r\nFirzzzt up, choose the slot you’d like to fill.
[Ctrl1:battle_oneline ]Let’s go ahead and drop [Name:PokemonNickname ]\ninto\r\nyour\r\nteam! Zzt!
Then we can fill all the rezzzt of the team with\nsome Auto Team Building, zzt-zzt!
And ta-da! You’ve got a Battle Team! Zzt-zzt!\c\nTry making some teamzzz yourself once you’re\ncomfortable with how this all works, OK?
Ranked Battles
In Ranked Battles, you can face off against other Trainers from\naround the world in the Single Battle or Double Battle format.\nEach season is a new chance to compete!
You’ll move up or down through the ranks based on the\nnumber of wins and losses you accumulate. If you reach the\nMaster Ball Tier, you’ll then compete with your fellow Trainers\nfor your final placement, which is based on your rating.
When each battle season ends, you’ll be able to receive\nrewards depending on the final rank you reached or how\nhigh you managed to place.
Once a new season starts, all results will be reset and\nevery Trainer will begin once more from the Poké Ball Tier.
The battle regulations will change each season, so be sure\nto check out all the details in the News announcements.
Casual Battles
In Casual Battles, you can face off against other Trainers from\naround the world in the Single Battle or Double Battle format.\nNo need to worry about winning or losing—these battles\nwon’t affect your current rank!
Single Battles
In [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Single Battles[System:Color a="255" ], you’ll select [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]three Pokémon[System:Color a="255" ] from your\nBattle Team, sending them out [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]one at a time[System:Color a="255" ] to do battle.\nVictory will go to the Trainer who first defeats all of their\nopponent’s Pokémon.
Select [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Fight [System:Color a="255" ]in the lower right-hand corner of the\nscreen to be taken to the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]move selection [System:Color a="255" ]screen.
Once you’ve reached the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]move selection[System:Color a="255" ] screen,\nselect [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Body Slam [System:Color a="255" ]from your Pokémon’s available [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]moves[System:Color a="255" ].\nIt’s time to dish out an attack on your opponent!
[~ 66]
In a Pokémon battle, the Pokémon on both sides\nwill unleash moves just like this, one after another.\nTry to defeat the opposing Trainer by [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]reducing the HP[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]of all their Pokémon to zero[System:Color a="255" ]!
Next up, let’s take a look at [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]type matchups[System:Color a="255" ], which\nare critical for getting the upper hand in a battle.\nEvery Pokémon and all the moves they use\nhave at least one [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]type[System:Color a="255" ] associated with them.
A [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Grass-type[System:Color a="255" ] Pokémon will take double the\ndamage if hit with a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Fire-type move[System:Color a="255" ].\nBut a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Fire-type[System:Color a="255" ] Pokémon will take just half\nthe damage if hit with a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Grass-type move[System:Color a="255" ].
These differences in the effectiveness of moves is how\ntype matchups play a role in Pokémon battles.
The Venusaur you’re up against has the Grass type.\nTry using a Fire-type move against it, now that you know\nhow effective Fire-type moves are against Grass types.\n\nSelect [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Fight[System:Color a="255" ], then go for [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Flamethrower[System:Color a="255" ]!
You defeated the Grass-type Venusaur using\nthe Fire-type move Flamethrower!\n\nUse type matchups to choose the most effective\nmoves possible and take control of your battles.
When a Pokémon [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]faints[System:Color a="255" ], a Trainer must then\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]switch in[System:Color a="255" ] another Pokémon from their party.\n\nYour next opponent appears to be the Water-type\nPokémon [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Blastoise[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nWater-type moves deal double damage against Fire-type\nPokémon, so your side is now at a disadvantage.
When you find yourself on the wrong end of an unfavorable\ntype matchup, switching your Pokémon out so you can send in\na different Pokémon to fight can be a good strategy.\nLet’s give it a try. Start by selecting [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Pokémon[System:Color a="255" ].
When you select [Character2:L_DoubleQuot. ][System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Pokémon[System:Color a="255" ],[Character2:R_DoubleQuot. ] you’ll be taken to another screen,\nwhere you can choose a different Pokémon to switch in.\nWhy don’t you select [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Meganium[System:Color a="255" ] and send it into this battle?
You switched in Meganium, which has a type advantage against\nBlastoise. Pokémon can’t use moves on the turn they switch in,\nbut since damage from Water-type moves is halved against\nGrass types, you were able to limit the damage you took.
Now let’s try having Meganium use [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Bullet Seed[System:Color a="255" ], a Grass-type\nmove that will deal double damage against Water types.
You defeated Blastoise!\n\nRemember that switching in different Pokémon during\na battle can be an effective tool for seizing victory.
Your opponent has now sent out [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Heracross[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nTry using the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Psychic-type move Zen Headbutt[System:Color a="255" ], which\ndeals double damage against [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Fighting-type Pokémon[System:Color a="255" ].
Whichever Pokémon has the higher [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Speed[System:Color a="255" ] stat\nwill usually get to move first each turn.\n\nYour opponent’s Heracross will be the first one to attack\nbecause it has a higher Speed stat than your Meganium.
In that case, why don’t you try switching in a\nspeedier Pokémon so you can attack first?\n\nGo ahead and switch in [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Pidgeot[System:Color a="255" ], which has a\nhigher Speed stat than Heracross.
Pidgeot is now in the battle, and since it has a\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]higher Speed [System:Color a="255" ]stat than the opposing Heracross,\nit should be able to attack first.\n\nTry having Pidgeot use its [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Hurricane[System:Color a="255" ] move!
Pidgeot’s Speed stat was higher than Heracross’s,\nso it was able to attack first and knock Heracross out!\n\nSince you managed to defeat all [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]three Pokémon[System:Color a="255" ]\nfrom the other side, that means you win this battle!\n\nNow, keep it up and have fun battling Pokémon!
Double Battles
In [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Double Battles[System:Color a="255" ], you and an opponent will each select\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]four Pokémon[System:Color a="255" ] from your Battle Teams, sending them out\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]two at a time[System:Color a="255" ] to do battle. Victory will go to the Trainer\nwho first defeats all of their opponent’s Pokémon.
These battles allow you to enjoy more challenging strategies.\nYou’ll need to remember the basics that apply to Single Battles\nwhile also making new decisions, like which of your\nopponent’s two Pokémon to target with your attacks.
In Double Battles, you get to choose [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]the actions for[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]two different Pokémon from your team each turn[System:Color a="255" ]. First,\nwe’ll start with [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Primarina[System:Color a="255" ]. Select [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Fight[System:Color a="255" ], then have\nPrimarina use its move [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Moonblast[System:Color a="255" ].
Since this is a Double Battle, you’ll need to choose\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]which Pokémon to target [System:Color a="255" ]after selecting a move.\nIn this case, go ahead and choose [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Snorlax[System:Color a="255" ].
Now let’s select an action for [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Garchomp[System:Color a="255" ] to take.\n\nThis time, how about using [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Rock Slide[System:Color a="255" ] to attack both of\nyour opponent’s Pokémon at once?\n\nSelect [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Fight[System:Color a="255" ] for your Garchomp and go for Rock Slide.\nThen choose both of the opposing Pokémon as the targets.
With Garchomp’s Rock Slide, you were able to attack\nboth of the opposing Pokémon at once.\n\nYou can sometimes seize the advantage in Double Battles by\nusing multitarget moves like this, so keep this strategy in mind!\n\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Note: Multitarget moves will deal less damage when used[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]against two targets than when they’re used against one target,[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]so make sure you take this into account.[System:Color a="255" ]
Mega Evolution
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Mega Evolution[System:Color a="255" ] is a mechanic only available to certain\nPokémon. It changes a Pokémon’s appearance, raises\nits overall stats, and has the potential to greatly expand\nthe strategies you employ in battle.
A [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Pokémon capable of Mega Evolution [System:Color a="255" ]can Mega Evolve\nif it’s holding a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Mega Stone [System:Color a="255" ]that’s specific to its species.
Your Charizard is a Pokémon that can Mega Evolve,\nand it’s holding a Mega Stone: [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Charizardite X[System:Color a="255" ]!
To have it Mega Evolve, first select [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Fight[System:Color a="255" ].
Next, choose the Mega Evolve option, then [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]select a move [System:Color a="255" ]to\ntrigger your Pokémon’s Mega Evolution. If you change your\nmind about Mega Evolving, you can also back out by choosing\nthe Mega Evolve option once more.
Now, why don’t you select the move [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Dragon Claw[System:Color a="255" ]\nafter choosing the Mega Evolve option?
Since Charizard Mega Evolved into [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Mega Charizard X[System:Color a="255" ]\nand had its stats raised, it was able to defeat Goodra!\n\nMega Evolution can only be used [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]one time per battle[System:Color a="255" ],\nso think carefully about which Pokémon you’ll want to\nMega Evolve and give them a Mega Stone to hold!
Move Priority
The order in which Pokémon use their moves is usually\ndetermined by which of them has the higher [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Speed [System:Color a="255" ]stat.\n\nTest this out by selecting [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Fight[System:Color a="255" ] and then having [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Lucario\n[System:Color a="255" ]use its [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Meteor Mash[System:Color a="255" ] move.
The opposing [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Alakazam[System:Color a="255" ] has a higher [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Speed [System:Color a="255" ]stat,\nso it was able to attack first.\n\nHowever, there are some moves that allow the user\nto act first even when facing speedier opponents.\n\nThese moves are described as having a high [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]priority[System:Color a="255" ],\nand they’re called [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]priority moves[System:Color a="255" ]. Moves with higher\npriority are used before moves with lower priority.
For any priority move, you can check [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]how high[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]its priority is[System:Color a="255" ] by selecting Fight, then looking at\nthe relevant number in the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Move Info[System:Color a="255" ] window that\ncan be displayed on the move selection screen.
To see for yourself what happens to the order of moves\nin a battle when you use a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]priority move[System:Color a="255" ], try having your\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Lucario[System:Color a="255" ] use [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Bullet Punch [System:Color a="255" ]this time.
Ta-da! Your Lucario was able to attack first, even though\nit was up against an opponent with a higher Speed stat.\n\nUse priority moves wisely to help your team stay\none step ahead of the opposition!
Physical vs. Special Moves
Attack moves can be either [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]physical moves [System:Color a="255" ]or [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]special moves[System:Color a="255" ].\nPhysical moves will do more damage the higher the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Attack [System:Color a="255" ]stat\nof the Pokémon using them. Special moves, on the other hand,\nwill do more damage the higher the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Sp. Atk [System:Color a="255" ]stat of the user.
But these moves aren’t impacted only by the user’s Attack\nor Sp. Atk stat. Physical moves will also deal LESS damage\nthe higher the target’s [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Defense [System:Color a="255" ]stat is. Likewise, special moves\nwill deal less damage if the target has a high [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Sp. Def[System:Color a="255" ] stat.
The [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Avalugg[System:Color a="255" ] you’re facing off against has a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]high Defense[System:Color a="255" ]\nstat but a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]low Sp. Def[System:Color a="255" ] stat.\n\nAs a test, try using [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Dragon Darts[System:Color a="255" ], which is a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]physical move[System:Color a="255" ].
Since the target has a high Defense stat, the attack didn’t\ndo all that much damage.\n\nNext, try using [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Dragon Pulse[System:Color a="255" ], which is a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]special move[System:Color a="255" ].
Because the target has a low Sp. Def stat, your Pokémon’s\nmove was able to deal a lot of damage.\n\nBut remember that it’s not only the target’s Defense and\nSp. Def stats that matter!\n\nPhysical moves will deal more damage when used by a\nPokémon with a high [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Attack [System:Color a="255" ]stat, while special moves will\ndeal more damage when used by a Pokémon with a high\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Sp. Atk[System:Color a="255" ] stat.
Take into account your Pokémon’s stats as well as\nthose of your opponent to determine whether a\nsituation calls for physical moves or special moves!
Status Conditions
If you inflict an opponent with a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]status condition[System:Color a="255" ],\nyou can quickly turn a battle to your advantage.\n\nTo see this effect in action, have [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Arcanine [System:Color a="255" ]use\nthe move [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Will-O-Wisp[System:Color a="255" ].
After the opponent used the physical move Close Combat,\nyour Will-O-Wisp inflicted them with a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]burn[System:Color a="255" ]! A burned\nPokémon’s [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]physical moves will have their damage halved[System:Color a="255" ],\nand the Pokémon will also [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]take damage at the end of the turn[System:Color a="255" ].
Let’s test for ourselves whether the opponent’s physical moves\nreally do only deal half as much damage as before, shall we?\n\nThis time, try choosing the move [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Flare Blitz[System:Color a="255" ].
Not only did the opponent’s physical move, Close Combat,\nhave its damage halved, but the opponent also fainted due to\nthe damage it took from its burn!\n\nRemember—inflicting status conditions on your opponents\nwill help you seize the upper hand in battles!
Contact vs. Noncontact Moves
Pokémon moves are broadly divided into two groups:\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]contact moves[System:Color a="255" ] and [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]noncontact moves[System:Color a="255" ]. You can see\nthis categorization in the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Move Info [System:Color a="255" ]window that can\nbe displayed on the move selection screen.
Let’s learn about the differences between contact moves\nand noncontact moves by seeing how they interact with an\nAbility that is triggered by contact moves.\n\nStart by having [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Maushold[System:Color a="255" ] here use [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Population Bomb[System:Color a="255" ].
Since Maushold came into contact with the opponent\nupon using a contact move, it took damage from that\nPokémon’s Ability, [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Rough Skin[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nAnd since Population Bomb is a multistrike move, Maushold\ntook damage each time it touched the opponent, adding up\nto quite a lot of damage by the end of the turn.
Next, why don’t you see how things turn out when you\nhave Maushold use the noncontact move [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Bullet Seed[System:Color a="255" ]?
Since that was a noncontact move, Maushold never\ntriggered its opponent’s Rough Skin Ability, meaning it\ntook no damage while attacking.\n\nRemember that contact moves and noncontact moves\ncan have different impacts as you choose the right move\nfor each situation in battle!
Weather Conditions
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Weather conditions[System:Color a="255" ] can have a big impact on a battle.\nLet’s take a look at a scenario in which [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]rain[System:Color a="255" ] will help\nturn the tide of battle in your favor!\n\nBefore we go changing the weather, though, it’s important\nto understand where we’re starting from. Let’s begin by\nhaving [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Basculegion[System:Color a="255" ] use its [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Wave Crash [System:Color a="255" ]move.
Oof, the damage from that Wave Crash didn’t even\nreduce the opposing Pokémon’s HP by half.\n\nBut what about if we try [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]changing the weather[System:Color a="255" ]?\nHave [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Basculegion[System:Color a="255" ] use its [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Rain Dance[System:Color a="255" ] move next.
The weather has changed to [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]rain[System:Color a="255" ]. When it’s raining,\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]the power of Water-type moves is boosted by 50%[System:Color a="255" ].
But that’s not all. Basculegion’s Ability [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Swift Swim[System:Color a="255" ]\nalso [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]doubles its Speed stat[System:Color a="255" ] when it’s [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]raining[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nWhy don’t you try that [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Wave Crash[System:Color a="255" ] again in this weather?
Thanks to the rain, that Water-type move had its power\nboosted by 50% and Basculegion had its Speed stat doubled\nby its Swift Swim Ability, meaning that it got to attack first!\n\nMake good use of the weather to help you\nturn the tides of battle in your favor!
Terrains
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Terrains[System:Color a="255" ] can have various useful effects, including boosting\nthe power of certain types of moves.\n\nTry having [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Hatterene[System:Color a="255" ] here use the move [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Psychic Terrain[System:Color a="255" ].
Your opponent used the priority move [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Extreme Speed[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nBut [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]priority moves fail[System:Color a="255" ] if Psychic Terrain is active.
Why don’t you have your Pokémon try the move [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Psychic[System:Color a="255" ]\nnow that Psychic Terrain is in effect?
The incoming Extreme Speed failed, and you also\nmanaged to knock out the opponent with your attack!\nThis was helped by the fact that [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]the power of Psychic-type[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]moves is boosted by 30% [System:Color a="255" ]while Psychic Terrain is active.\n\nTerrains have all kinds of effects that impact both your side\nand your opponent’s side. Use them to your advantage!

Text File : btl_condition

The Pokémon has a 12.5% chance of\nbeing unable to use moves. Its Speed\nstat is also halved.
The Pokémon can’t use almost any moves but has\na 25% chance of being cured each time it tries\nto do so. The Pokémon will be cured on its third\nturn after becoming frozen or if it takes damage\nfrom a Fire-type move or certain other moves.
The Pokémon takes damage equal to 1/16\nof its max HP at the end of every turn.\nThe damage dealt by its physical moves\nis also halved.
The Pokémon takes damage equal to 1/8 of its\nmax HP at the end of every turn.
The Pokémon takes increasing poison damage\nat the end of every turn, starting at 1/16 of the\nPokémon’s max HP, then 2/16, then 3/16, and\nso on. If the Pokémon switches out and reenters\nbattle, the damage restarts at 1/16 of its max HP.
The Pokémon can’t use moves other than Snore\nor Sleep Talk. After a Pokémon is put to sleep, it\nwill remain asleep on its first turn, it will have a\n1-in-3 chance of being cured on its second turn,\nand it will be cured on its third turn. A Pokémon\nthat used the move Rest has no chance of being\ncured until its third turn.

Text File : btl_state_syn
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
Boosts the damage dealt by Fire-type moves\nby 50% and halves the damage dealt by\nWater-type moves.
Harsh Sunlight
Boosts the damage dealt by Water-type moves\nby 50% and halves the damage dealt by\nFire-type moves.
Rain
Pokémon that are not Rock, Ground, or Steel\ntypes take damage equal to 1/16 of their max\nHP at the end of every turn. Boosts the Sp. Def\nstats of Rock-type Pokémon by 50%.
Sandstorm
Boosts the Defense stats of Ice-type Pokémon by\n50%.
Snow
Pokémon on the ground have the power of their\nElectric-type moves boosted by 30% and they\ncannot fall asleep.
Electric Terrain
Pokémon on the ground have the power of their\nGrass-type moves boosted by 30% and they\nhave 1/16 of their max HP restored at the end\nof every turn.
Grassy Terrain
Pokémon on the ground have the power of their\nDragon-type moves halved, they are immune to\nstatus conditions, and they cannot become\nconfused.
Misty Terrain
Pokémon with lower Speed stats move first.
Trick Room
Most held items do not work.
Magic Room
Pokémon’s Defense and Sp. Def stats\nare swapped.
Wonder Room
The Pokémon’s attacks are more likely to be\ncritical hits.
Critical-Hit Ratio Boost
For 1–4 turns, the Pokémon has a 1-in-3 chance\nof hurting itself.
Confused
The Pokémon has a 50% chance of being unable\nto use its moves while the Pokémon that gave it\nthe Infatuated status is on the field.
Infatuated
The Pokémon will fall asleep at the end of the\nnext turn after becoming drowsy.
Drowsy
[Ctrl1:battle_oneline ]The Pokémon can only use\n[Name:Move ].
The Pokémon can only use whichever move it last\nused before gaining the Encore status.
Encore
The Pokémon’s Ability loses its effect.
No Ability
The Pokémon cannot use the same move twice\nin a row.
Unable to Repeat
Doubles the Pokémon’s Speed stat.
Tailwind
[Name:Move ] cannot be used.
Move Disabled
The Pokémon cannot use whichever move it last\nused before gaining the Move Disabled status.
The Pokémon cannot be switched out of battle.
Can’t Escape
On the next turn after gaining the Locked On\nstatus, the Pokémon’s move will not miss if\ntargeting the Pokémon that was locked onto.
Locked On
The power of the next Electric-type move used\nby the Pokémon will be doubled.
Electric Boost
Boosts the accuracy of moves by 67%. Pokémon\nsuch as Flying types or ones with the Levitate\nAbility become grounded. Moves that involve\nflying or leaping cannot be used.
Gravity
The Pokémon is immune to status conditions and\ncannot become confused.
Safeguard
Pokémon that switch into battle will take damage\nequal to 1/8 of their max HP. This damage differs\ndepending on the Pokémon’s type matchup with\nthe Rock type.
Stealth Rock
The Pokémon’s Defense and Sp. Def stats are\nboosted by 1 stage for each time it has used\nStockpile.
Stockpiling
The Pokémon can use only attacks.
Taunted
The Pokémon floats off the ground, making it\nimmune to Ground-type moves, as well as the\nSpikes, Toxic Spikes, and Sticky Web statuses.
Magnet Rise
Pokémon that switch into battle will be poisoned\nor, if 2 layers of Toxic Spikes are set, badly\npoisoned. Pokémon such as Flying types or ones\nwith the Levitate Ability are unaffected.
Toxic Spikes
At the end of the next turn after the Wish status\nis activated, the HP of the Pokémon in the\naffected spot will be restored by 1/2 of the max\nHP of the Pokémon that caused the status.
Wish
Pokémon that switch into battle will have their\nSpeed stats lowered by 1 stage. Pokémon such as\nFlying types or ones with the Levitate Ability\nare unaffected.
Sticky Web
The Pokémon has 1/16 of its max HP restored at\nthe end of every turn. It also becomes grounded\nand cannot be switched out of battle.
Ingrained
The Pokémon loses 1/4 of its max HP at the end\nof every turn.
Cursed
The Pokémon gains the Ghost type.
Trick-or-Treating
Halves the damage taken from special moves.\nIn Double Battles, this damage is reduced by\n1/3 instead.
Light Screen
Halves the damage taken from physical moves.\nIn Double Battles, this damage is reduced by\n1/3 instead.
Reflect
Any moves known by the Pokémon that caused\nthis status cannot be used by its opponents.
Sealing Off
The Pokémon will faint 3 turns after gaining the\nPerishing status.
Perishing
Pokémon that switch into battle will take damage\nequal to 1/8 of their max HP. This damage will\nincrease if 2 layers of Spikes are set, and again\nif 3 layers are set. Pokémon such as Flying types\nor ones with the Levitate Ability are unaffected.
Spikes
If the Pokémon is knocked out by an opponent,\nthat opponent will also be knocked out.
Destiny Bound
The Pokémon gains the Grass type.
Forest Cursed
The Pokémon takes damage equal to 1/8 of\nits max HP at the end of every turn. Whichever\nPokémon is in the spot of the Pokémon that\ncaused the Leech Seeded status has its HP\nrestored by the same amount.
Leech Seeded
For 4–5 turns, the Pokémon takes damage equal\nto 1/8 of its max HP at the end of every turn. It\ncannot be switched out of battle.
Bound
For 2–3 turns, the Pokémon continues its attack\nand is unable to take any other actions. After\nthat, it becomes confused.
Rampaging
The Pokémon takes increasing poison damage\nat the end of every turn, starting at 1/16 of the\nPokémon’s max HP, then 2/16, then 3/16, and\nso on. If the Pokémon switches out and reenters\nbattle, the damage restarts at 1/16 of its max HP.
Badly Poisoned
The Pokémon in the targeted spot will take\ndamage 2 turns after the Future Attack status\nis activated.
Future Attack
For 3 turns, the Pokémon continues its attack and\nis unable to take any other actions. During this\ntime, no Pokémon on the field can fall asleep.
Uproar
The Pokémon has 1/16 of its max HP restored at\nthe end of every turn.
Aqua Ring
The Pokémon is now grounded and can be\naffected by Ground-type moves.
Landed
No Pokémon on the field can be switched out\nof battle until the end of the next turn after the\nFairy Locked status is activated.
Fairy Locked

Syrupy

Healing Prevented
[~ 134]
[~ 135]
The Pokémon cannot take any actions for 1 turn.
Recharging
The Pokémon spends 1 turn charging before\nusing a move.
Charging
The Pokémon cannot be hit by most moves,\nexcluding moves such as Thunder, Hurricane,\nand Smack Down. The Pokémon is also\nunaffected by the terrain.
Sky-High
The Pokémon cannot be hit by most moves, but\nSurf and Whirlpool will hit and will deal double\ndamage. The Pokémon is also unaffected by\nthe terrain.
Submerged
The Pokémon cannot be hit by most moves, but\nEarthquake will hit and will deal double damage.\nThe Pokémon is also unaffected by the terrain.
Underground
The Pokémon cannot be hit by moves and is\nunaffected by the terrain.
Concealed
Moves such as Supercell Slam, Body Slam,\nDragon Rush, Flying Press, Heat Crash, and\nHeavy Slam will not miss the Pokémon and\nwill deal double damage.
Minimized
