Text File : help_syn
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
Gameplay Guides
[Digit:2digits ]/[Digit:2digits Idx="1" ]
Battling Online
Recruit Pokémon
You can gain new Pokémon for your teams\nby [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]recruiting [System:Color a="255" ]them from available lineups.
You’ll be able to meet a new lineup of Pokémon\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]for 0 VP every 22 hours[System:Color a="255" ]. Then you can pick one\nPokémon from that lineup to recruit.
For more details, check out the section titled [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Recruiting[System:Color a="255" ].
Bring Visitors from Pokémon HOME
The Pokémon you have in Pokémon HOME can be\nbrought over to Pokémon Champions as [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]visitors[System:Color a="255" ].
For more details, check out the section titled [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Recruiting[System:Color a="255" ].
Train Your Pokémon
Through [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]training[System:Color a="255" ], you can make changes to your Pokémon’s\nstat points, stat alignment, moves, Abilities, and more.
For more details, check out the section titled [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Training[System:Color a="255" ].
Build Battle Teams
Before you start battling other Trainers, you’ll need to\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]build a Battle Team[System:Color a="255" ]—or more than one, if you like!\n\nEach Battle Team is made up of six Pokémon.
Consider which battle strategies you’d like to use.\nThat should help you decide which six Pokémon\nto put on each of your Battle Teams.
For more details, check out the section titled [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Your Box[System:Color a="255" ].
Get Battling!
Once you’ve made at least one Battle Team, you can [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]try out[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Ranked Battles[System:Color a="255" ] to earn VP and move up through the ranks.
The World of Battling
Ranked Battles
In [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Ranked Battles[System:Color a="255" ], you can face off against\nother Trainers from around the world.
The Ranked Battle system divides Trainers into ranks\nthat indicate their strength. [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Trainers can move up or down[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]the ranks depending on how well they do in battle.[System:Color a="255" ]
When you take part in Ranked Battles, you’ll be matched\nwith [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]other Trainers in similar ranks[System:Color a="255" ] so you can enjoy\nthrilling matches against those of similar skill level.
Casual Battles
In [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Casual Battles[System:Color a="255" ], you can face off against\nother Trainers from around the world.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]You won’t move up or down the ranks based on[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]how well you do[System:Color a="255" ] in Casual Battles.
And unlike Ranked Battles, Casual Battles [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]won’t[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]earn you any VP for your battle efforts[System:Color a="255" ].
Private Battles
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Private Battles[System:Color a="255" ] allow you to create a room of your own to\nenjoy battling with your friends or other Trainers using\nbattle rules of your choice.
Trainers can join a room by [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]entering the correct Room ID[System:Color a="255" ].
[~ 31]
Once you’re in the room, you can choose to battle or to\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]spectate[System:Color a="255" ] if you’d rather just watch the battles taking place.
Single Battles
In [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Single Battles[System:Color a="255" ], you and an opponent will each send out\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]one Pokémon at a time[System:Color a="255" ] to do battle. Victory will go to the\nTrainer who first defeats all of their opponent’s Pokémon.
Check out the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]battle tutorial on Single Battles [System:Color a="255" ]to learn\nmore about them through a hands-on demonstration.
Double Battles
In [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Double Battles[System:Color a="255" ], you and an opponent will each send out\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]two Pokémon at a time[System:Color a="255" ] to do battle. Victory will go to the\nTrainer who first defeats all of their opponent’s Pokémon.
The same basic elements that are at play in a Single Battle\nstill apply, but in a Double Battle, you will need to\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]select actions for two Pokémon each turn[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nThere are also certain moves better suited to Double Battles,\nsuch as moves that can hit multiple Pokémon at once, so you’ll\nwant to learn how to tailor your strategy to this format.
Check out the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]battle tutorial on Double Battles [System:Color a="255" ]to learn\nmore about them through a hands-on demonstration.
Ranks
Your [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]wins and losses [System:Color a="255" ]in Ranked Battles will\ncause you to [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]move up and down the ranks[System:Color a="255" ].
Ranks are grouped into different tiers, as below.\n ・ The Beginner Tier (only a single rank)\n ・ The Poké Ball Tier (from rank 4 to 1)\n ・ The Great Ball Tier (from rank 4 to 1)\n ・ The Ultra Ball Tier (from rank 4 to 1)\n ・ The Master Ball Tier (from rank 4 to 1)\nIf you reach the Master Ball Tier, you’ll [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]compete with other[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Trainers for your final placement, which is based on your rating[System:Color a="255" ].
Finally, if you exceed a certain placement in the\nMaster Ball Tier, you’ll enter the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Champion Tier[System:Color a="255" ].
Depending on how well you did in the previous season,\nyou may even receive a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]performance bonus[System:Color a="255" ] that will\nmake it easier to climb the ranks in the new season.
Seasons
Ranked Battles take place during set periods known as [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]seasons[System:Color a="255" ].
When a season ends, [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]you can receive rewards based on[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]the rank you reached or the placement you achieved[System:Color a="255" ].
When a new season begins, your results will be reset\nand you will start again from the Poké Ball Tier.\n\nThe regulations also change each season, so you’ll\nwant to check all the details in the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]News[System:Color a="255" ].
Regulations
Regulations are the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]rules that govern things like which[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Pokémon species and held items are allowed in battle[System:Color a="255" ].
Online Competitions
With Online Competitions, you can take part in all kinds of\nopportunities to battle others.\n\nSome competitions [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]offer special rewards[System:Color a="255" ] too!
To take part in Online Competitions, you’ll [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]need to[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]enter the competition [System:Color a="255" ]in advance.\n\nOnce you’ve entered a competition, you’ll be able to\nbattle your fellow entrants for the length of the event\nperiod.
Use the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Check Rules [System:Color a="255" ]button when viewing a competition to\nlearn more about the rules governing that competition.
Battle Data
With the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Battle Data [System:Color a="255" ]feature, you can check the results\nof competitions and Ranked Battles seasons.
For each season or competition, you’ll be able to view:\n [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]・ Rankings of all the Trainers who took part[System:Color a="255" ]\n [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]・ Rankings of your friends who took part[System:Color a="255" ]\n [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]・ Rankings of the Pokémon that were used the most[System:Color a="255" ]
You can also check the results of past competitions\nand Ranked Battles seasons there.
Mechanics
Mega Evolution
Certain Pokémon are able to [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Mega Evolve[System:Color a="255" ] during battles.\n\nMega-Evolved Pokémon have their stats greatly increased\nand their types or Abilities may also change.
In order to Mega Evolve, a Pokémon must be holding\na [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Mega Stone[System:Color a="255" ] that’s specific to its species.\n\nIt is only possible to trigger Mega Evolution once per battle.
Check out the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]battle tutorial on Mega Evolution [System:Color a="255" ]to learn\nmore about it through a hands-on demonstration.
Your Box
Building Battle Teams
Within your Box, you can [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]build Battle Teams[System:Color a="255" ].
You cannot put two of the same species of Pokémon in\na Battle Team.\n\nAnd you must have six Pokémon total on a Battle Team\nin order to take part in battles.
Auto Team Build
If you use [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Auto Team Build[System:Color a="255" ], a balanced team will be\ncreated for you automatically, using the Pokémon and\nheld items that you have available.
The team will [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]not include [System:Color a="255" ]any Pokémon or held items\nthat are not allowed in the current Ranked Battles season.
Limits on Your Box & Battle Teams
When you first begin playing the game, your Box will only\nbe able to hold a maximum of [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]30 Pokémon[System:Color a="255" ]. This limit can be\nexpanded by either [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]reaching a higher rank in Ranked Battles or[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]purchasing a membership[System:Color a="255" ].
You can have up to [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]three Battle Teams[System:Color a="255" ] at one time.\nIf you purchase a membership, you’ll instead be able\nto have a maximum of [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]18 Battle Teams[System:Color a="255" ].
For more details, check out the section titled [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Other[System:Color a="255" ],\nand within it, find the subsection on [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Membership[System:Color a="255" ].
Held Items
Giving [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]held items [System:Color a="255" ]to your Pokémon can cause a variety\nof effects to occur during battle.\n\nWhile building your Battle Teams, you’ll be able to\ngive [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]each Pokémon a single item[System:Color a="255" ] to hold.
Note that you cannot give the same held item to more than\none Pokémon on the same Battle Team.
Favorites
Pokémon can be [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]favorited[System:Color a="255" ].
Favoriting a Pokémon will help you prevent it from\nbeing accidentally returned to Roster Ranch.
Labels
Pokémon can be given [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]labels[System:Color a="255" ].
The following elements of a label are customizable.\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ] ・ Name[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ] ・ Icon[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ] ・ Color[System:Color a="255" ]
Sorting
The [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Sort[System:Color a="255" ] function makes it possible to reorder your Pokémon\nby the date you acquired them, their Pokédex number, their\nspecies name, or how recently you’ve used them.
Filtering
The [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Filter[System:Color a="255" ] function lets you narrow down your Pokémon\nby parameters such as their species name, type,\nor whether they’ve been favorited or labeled.
Training
Training Overview
With the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Training[System:Color a="255" ] feature, you can change your Pokémon’s\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]stat points[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]stat alignments[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]moves[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Abilities[System:Color a="255" ], and more.
Stat Points
You can change your Pokémon’s stats by\ndistributing what are known as [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]stat points[System:Color a="255" ].
Each stat can be given [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]32 [System:Color a="255" ]stat points at most.\n\nIn total, [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]66[System:Color a="255" ] stat points are available to be distributed\nacross all the stats of a single Pokémon.
Stat Alignment
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Stat alignments [System:Color a="255" ]typically raise one stat and lower another.
The raised stat will be [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]increased by 10%[System:Color a="255" ], while the\nlowered stat will be [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]decreased by 10%[System:Color a="255" ].
Moves
Each Pokémon [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]can learn up to four moves[System:Color a="255" ].
Select an empty move slot or a move that you want to replace,\nand then select the move you want your Pokémon to learn.\n\nYou can also have your Pokémon [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]forget moves[System:Color a="255" ].
Abilities
Pokémon have [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Abilities[System:Color a="255" ], which can cause a variety\nof effects to occur during battle.\n\nOnly one Ability can be selected for each Pokémon.
Replica Teams
With the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Replica Team[System:Color a="255" ] feature, you can input the Team ID\nof a team that has been shared, and a Battle Team based\non that team will be automatically created for you.
Your Pokémon can be [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]trained up all at once [System:Color a="255" ]in order to\ngive them the same stat points, stat alignments, moves,\nand Abilities as the Pokémon in the shared team.
Even if you [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]don’t have all the Pokémon needed [System:Color a="255" ]to replicate\na particular team, training can still be carried out on the\nPokémon that you do have.
You can also share Battle Teams that you’ve created.
Battle Tutorials
In the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]battle tutorials[System:Color a="255" ], you’ll learn the basics of Pokémon\nbattling as you’re led step-by-step through [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]hands-on[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]demonstrations [System:Color a="255" ]of a variety of topics.
You’ll [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]receive a reward the first time you complete each[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]tutorial[System:Color a="255" ], so definitely consider checking them out!
Recruiting
Recruiting Pokémon
You can gain new Pokémon for your teams\nby [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]recruiting[System:Color a="255" ] them from available lineups.
You’ll be able to meet a new lineup of Pokémon\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]for 0 VP every 22 hours[System:Color a="255" ]. Then you can pick one\nPokémon from that lineup to recruit.
You can also use VP or Quick Coupons to [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]reduce the time[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]you have to wait[System:Color a="255" ] before you can recruit another Pokémon.
There are some Pokémon that can only be recruited once.\nYou won’t be able to meet these Pokémon again in a future\nlineup even if you return them to Roster Ranch, so make sure\nyou’re absolutely certain about returning them before doing so.
Pokémon Rosters
Each [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]roster[System:Color a="255" ] contains a different variety of Pokémon.\nYou can meet these Pokémon via lineups, which are\nsmaller groups selected at random from the roster.
Note that some rosters will allow you to recruit\nPokémon [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]using tickets instead of VP[System:Color a="255" ].
Different Ways to Recruit
There are two ways to recruit a Pokémon:\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]trial recruitment[System:Color a="255" ] and [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]permanent recruitment[System:Color a="255" ].
You can recruit Pokémon on a trial basis for [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]0 VP[System:Color a="255" ], but this\ncomes with [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]certain restrictions[System:Color a="255" ]. For example, you won’t be\nable to train Pokémon recruited this way, and you can only\nadd them to your Battle Teams for a limited time.
Recruiting Pokémon permanently means [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]spending VP[System:Color a="255" ], but\nthese Pokémon will be [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]free from any restrictions[System:Color a="255" ]. You’ll be\nable to train permanently recruited Pokémon, and you can\nadd them to Battle Teams for as long as you like.
Returning Pokémon
The Pokémon you recruit can be [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]returned to Roster Ranch[System:Color a="255" ].\n\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Once a Pokémon has been returned, you cannot get it back![System:Color a="255" ]
You can return up to [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]30 Pokémon[System:Color a="255" ] at one time.\n\nAny items held by Pokémon will be removed\nwhen you return them to Roster Ranch.
Linking to Pokémon HOME
The Pokémon you have in Pokémon HOME can be sent to\nPokémon Champions as [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]visitors[System:Color a="255" ].
When you collect a Pokémon that is visiting this game from\nPokémon HOME for the first time, that Pokémon’s current\nstrength will be used to determine its strength in Pokémon\nChampions.\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Note: ”Strength” in Pokémon Champions refers to a Pokémon’s[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]stat points, stat alignment, moves, Ability, and other such things.[System:Color a="255" ]
If a Pokémon knows moves that cannot be used in Pokémon\nChampions, you’ll need to change those moves via training.
Pokémon you’ve brought over to visit from Pokémon HOME\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]can be sent back to Pokémon HOME[System:Color a="255" ].
Training done here won’t carry over to Pokémon HOME, but\nif the same Pokémon visit Pokémon Champions again, [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]their[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]strength from the last time they visited will be retained, and[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]any titles they received in Pokémon Champions will be saved[System:Color a="255" ].
If a Pokémon is sent back to Pokémon HOME [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]and its strength[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]is changed in a different game, this new strength will not carry[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]over into Pokémon Champions [System:Color a="255" ]even if the Pokémon visits this\ngame again. However, any titles that a Pokémon newly receives\nin other games will carry over into Pokémon Champions.
Note that if a Pokémon is sent back to Pokémon HOME and\nthen returns to visit Pokémon Champions [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]in a different form[System:Color a="255" ],\nthe [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]results of any training[System:Color a="255" ] that Pokémon had undergone in\nPokémon Champions will be [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]lost[System:Color a="255" ].\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Note: Any titles received in Pokémon Champions will be saved.[System:Color a="255" ]
Sending Pokémon Back to Pokémon HOME
Pokémon you’ve brought over to visit from Pokémon HOME\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]can be sent back to Pokémon HOME at any time[System:Color a="255" ].
Training done here [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]won’t carry over to Pokémon HOME[System:Color a="255" ], but if\nthe same Pokémon visit Pokémon Champions again, any training\nthey received here [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]will be saved[System:Color a="255" ].
Note that if a Pokémon leaves Pokémon Champions and then\nreturns [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]in a different form, the results of any training that[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Pokémon had undergone in Pokémon Champions will be lost[System:Color a="255" ].
The Shop and Style Screens
The Shop Screen
The Shop screen is divided into two sections:\nthe [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Premium Shop [System:Color a="255" ]and the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Frontier Shop[System:Color a="255" ].
In the Premium Shop, you can purchase [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]memberships[System:Color a="255" ]\nand [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Premium Battle Passes[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nIn the Frontier Shop, you can exchange your VP for\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]held items[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]new clothes[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]poses[System:Color a="255" ], and more.
The Style Screen
On the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Style[System:Color a="255" ] screen, you can change your clothing,\nyour hair and cosmetics, the pose you strike when\nentering battle, and more.
Put together a combination that’s all your own,\nthen save it as a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]preset[System:Color a="255" ] style.
Wardrobe and Hair & Cosmetics
On the Style screen, you’ll find a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]wardrobe[System:Color a="255" ] where you can\nchange up your clothes and accessories, and you’ll find [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]hair[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]and cosmetics [System:Color a="255" ]options such as hairstyles and color contacts.
Throwing Styles, Pre-Battle Poses, and Victory Poses
These options let you choose [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]how you[System:Color a="255" ] [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]throw your\nPoké Balls [System:Color a="255" ]in battles, as well as [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]the poses you strike[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]when entering or winning battles[System:Color a="255" ].
Your Profile
On your [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Profile[System:Color a="255" ] screen, you can view information such as\nyour [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Trainer ID[System:Color a="255" ] and [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]gameplay stats[System:Color a="255" ]. You can also change up\nyour [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]badges[System:Color a="255" ], your [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Trainer icon[System:Color a="255" ], and your [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]title[System:Color a="255" ].
Each Trainer’s profile can be [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]viewed by other Trainers[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nYou can choose [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]how much information to make public[System:Color a="255" ]\nfrom the game’s Settings screen.
Badges, Titles, and Trainer Icons
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Badges[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]titles[System:Color a="255" ], and [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Trainer icons[System:Color a="255" ] can be earned by\nfulfilling certain conditions.
You can select [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]up to three[System:Color a="255" ] badges to display at a time.\n\nAs for titles and Trainer icons, you can select [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]just one[System:Color a="255" ].
Blocking Others
You can block other Trainers when viewing their profile.
When you block a Trainer, they’ll no longer be able to join\nany rooms you create for Private Battles.
The other Trainer will not be notified that you have blocked\nthem, nor will they be able to see that you have done so.
Achievements
There are two different kinds of achievements:\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Trainer achievements[System:Color a="255" ] and [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Pokémon achievements[System:Color a="255" ].
Fulfilling the conditions of these achievements\nwill earn you a variety of [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]rewards[System:Color a="255" ].
Trainer achievements are unlocked [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]by your progress[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]in areas such as battling and training[System:Color a="255" ].
Pokémon achievements are unlocked by [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]winning battles\nwhen using certain Pokémon[System:Color a="255" ].
Battle Passes and Cordy’s Missions
Battle Passes
A [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Battle Pass[System:Color a="255" ] allows you to obtain rewards as you\naccumulate [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Season Points (SP)[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nYou can earn [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]SP[System:Color a="255" ] by taking part in Ranked Battles,\namong other things.
Each Battle Pass is valid for a certain period of time. New Battle\nPasses become available with each new Ranked Battles season.
Premium Battle Passes
There are two varieties of Battle Pass: a regular\nBattle Pass and a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Premium Battle Pass[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nWith a Premium Battle Pass, you can [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]obtain rewards[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]that you cannot get with a regular Battle Pass[System:Color a="255" ].
Premium Battle Passes can be [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]purchased in the[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Premium Shop[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nIf you purchase a Premium Battle Pass, you’ll receive\nthe Premium Battle Pass rewards for all the Battle Pass\nlevels you’ve already attained.
Battle Passes and Premium Battle Passes are both valid for the\nsame period of time between fixed dates.\n\nIf you purchase a Premium Battle Pass, it will expire at the end\nof the Battle Pass period in which it was purchased. To receive\nPremium Battle Pass exclusive rewards for a new period, you can\npurchase the Premium Battle Pass for the new period.
Cordy’s Missions
With Cordy’s missions, you can earn rewards by fulfilling\ncertain conditions.
There are three categories of missions: [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]daily[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]weekly[System:Color a="255" ], and\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]starter[System:Color a="255" ] missions.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Daily missions[System:Color a="255" ] are updated [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]each day[System:Color a="255" ], while [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]weekly missions\n[System:Color a="255" ]are updated [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]once a week[System:Color a="255" ], giving you plenty of chances to\nfulfill different tasks to earn new rewards.
The [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]starter missions [System:Color a="255" ]can only be completed once—they\nwon’t be updated or offer new rewards after that.
Some of Cordy’s missions offer the option to [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]reroll[System:Color a="255" ],\nmeaning you can replace a mission with a new one.\n\nIf you do choose to [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]reroll[System:Color a="255" ], you’ll lose whatever progress\nyou had made on that mission, but you’ll be able to change\nto a mission with different fulfillment conditions.
The Submenu
Your Mailbox
Your [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]mailbox[System:Color a="255" ] is where you’ll find unclaimed rewards from\nyour Battle Pass or Cordy’s missions, gifts and messages\nfrom the organization that runs Frontier’s battles, and more.
Messages, gifts, and rewards have an expiration date.\n\nThey’ll be deleted after this date passes, so be sure\nto read your messages and claim your gifts and rewards\nfrequently to prevent this from happening.
All of the battles and events that take place here in the\ncity of Frontier are managed and operated by the\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Battle Stadium Organization[System:Color a="255" ], also known as the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]BSO[System:Color a="255" ].
Friends
If you become [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]friends[System:Color a="255" ] with another Trainer, you and that Trainer\nwill be able to view each other’s profiles.
Trainers you befriend can be invited to the rooms you\ncreate for Private Battles.\n\nInvited Trainers will be able to [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]join your room without[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]having to input the Room ID[System:Color a="255" ].
Your Block List
Your block list shows the names of Trainers you have blocked.\n\nTo block a Trainer, use the option you can find when viewing\ntheir profile.
If you block another Trainer, they will [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]not appear on your friend[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]list[System:Color a="255" ] even if they send you a friend request.
Blocked Trainers are [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]unable to join any Private Battle rooms[System:Color a="255" ]\ncreated by the Trainer who blocked them.
News
Check the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]News[System:Color a="255" ] to view the latest information about Pokémon\nChampions, upcoming events, and more.
You’ll see news that’s relevant for the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]region and location[System:Color a="255" ]\nyou have set as your current residence.
Settings
In the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Settings[System:Color a="255" ], you can tailor or change a variety of\noptions to suit your preferences.\n\nLet’s take a look at a couple of those options here.
Battle:\n [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]・ Display Battle Names[System:Color a="255" ]\nThis option lets you choose whether Pokémon’s battle\nnames are displayed, or only their species names.\n\n [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]・ Display Battle Info[System:Color a="255" ]\nThis option lets you choose whether statuses currently\naffecting the field are displayed during battles.
Mystery Gifts
The [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Mystery Gifts[System:Color a="255" ] feature allows you to claim gifts\nby inputting a code or password.
Pokémon
Stats
Pokémon have six stats: [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]HP[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Attack[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Defense[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Sp. Atk[System:Color a="255" ],\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Sp. Def[System:Color a="255" ], and [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Speed[System:Color a="255" ].
HP, Attack, and Defense
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]HP[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThis number tells you how much damage your Pokémon\ncan withstand.\n\nA Pokémon’s HP will go down when it takes damage.\nOnce its HP reaches zero, the Pokémon will faint.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Attack[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThis number gives you an idea of how much damage\nyour Pokémon can deal when it uses a physical move.\n\nThe higher the number, the more damage your Pokémon’s\nphysical moves will deal to targets.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Defense[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThis number gives you an idea of how much damage\nyour Pokémon can mitigate when hit by a physical move.\n\nThe higher the number, the less damage your Pokémon will\ntake from physical moves.
Sp. Atk, Sp. Def, and Speed
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Sp. Atk[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThis number gives you an idea of how much damage\nyour Pokémon can deal when it uses a special move.\n\nThe higher the number, the more damage your Pokémon’s\nspecial moves will deal to targets.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Sp. Def[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThis number gives you an idea of how much damage\nyour Pokémon can mitigate when hit by a special move.\n\nThe higher the number, the less damage your Pokémon will\ntake from special moves.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Speed[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThis number gives you an idea of the order in which\nPokémon will move in battle.\n\nThe Pokémon with the highest Speed stat will usually get to\nmove first. If two Pokémon have the same Speed stat, then\nthe order in which those Pokémon move will be random.
Stat Points
You can change your Pokémon’s stats by redistributing\ntheir [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]stat points [System:Color a="255" ]via training.
Each stat can be given [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]32 [System:Color a="255" ]stat points at most.\n\nIn total, [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]66[System:Color a="255" ] stat points are available to be distributed\nacross all the stats of a single Pokémon.
If you aren’t sure how to best distribute these stat points,\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]try giving the max 32 points to two stats that are naturally[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]high for your Pokémon[System:Color a="255" ].
Stat Alignment
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Stat alignments [System:Color a="255" ]typically raise one stat and lower another.
The raised stat will be [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]increased by 10%[System:Color a="255" ], while the\nlowered stat will be [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]decreased by 10%[System:Color a="255" ].
The stats that can be impacted by stat alignment are\nAttack, Defense, Sp. Atk, Sp. Def, and Speed.\n\nMost alignments raise [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]one[System:Color a="255" ] stat and lower [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]another[System:Color a="255" ], but not\nevery alignment will have such an effect.
If you aren’t sure which alignment would be best, choose one\nthat will [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]raise your Pokémon’s highest stat[System:Color a="255" ], then consider what\nmoves they use. If they [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]don’t use physical moves, lower their[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Attack[System:Color a="255" ]. If they [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]don’t use special moves, lower their Sp. Atk[System:Color a="255" ].
Abilities
Pokémon have [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Abilities[System:Color a="255" ], which can cause a variety of\neffects to occur during battle.
Held Items
Giving [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]held items[System:Color a="255" ] to your Pokémon can cause a variety\nof effects to occur during battle.
While building your Battle Teams, you’ll be able to\ngive each Pokémon a[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ] single [System:Color a="255" ]item to hold.
Moves
Pokémon can learn up to four [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]moves[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nImportant factors to consider about moves are their\npower, accuracy, PP, and additional effects.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Power[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThis number gives you an idea of how much damage a\nmove will deal to a target.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Accuracy[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThis number helps you understand the likelihood that a\nmove will successfully hit its target.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]PP[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThis number indicates how many times a move can be used\nin a single battle.
When a move’s PP drops to zero, you will be unable to\nuse that move for the remainder of the battle.\n\nIf you become unable to use any of your Pokémon’s\nmoves, it will automatically use a move called Struggle.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Additional Effects[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nSome moves can have a variety of additional effects\non top of dealing damage to a target.
Pokémon Titles
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Titles [System:Color a="255" ]are additional names—a sort of nickname that\nPokémon can have.\n\nIf a Pokémon has a title, it will be displayed when that\nPokémon enters a battle.
You can select a title for your Pokémon from its [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]summary[System:Color a="255" ] page.
When recruiting, you may find Pokémon that\nhave [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]titles[System:Color a="255" ] already.
Forms
Pokémon of the same species can sometimes come\nin [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]different forms[System:Color a="255" ].
When building a Battle Team, you are allowed to add only\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]a single Pokémon of each species[System:Color a="255" ].\n\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Even if they have different forms, you cannot put multiple[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Pokémon of the same species on the same Battle Team.[System:Color a="255" ]
Basic Battling Know-How
Type Matchups
There are 18 types in total. The damage that is dealt by any\ngiven move will be affected by how the move’s type matches up\nwith the type or types of the target Pokémon.
How types interact with each other is referred to as a\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]type matchup[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nWe’ll start by introducing three possible type matchups:\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]super effective[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]not very effective[System:Color a="255" ], and [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]has no effect[System:Color a="255" ].
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Super Effective[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nAn attack that is super effective will deal [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]double damage[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nExample:\nWhen the Grass-type Pokémon Venusaur is attacked with\nthe Fire-type move Flamethrower.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Not Very Effective [System:Color a="255" ]\n\nAn attack that is not very effective will deal [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]half as much[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]damage[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nExample:\nWhen the Grass-type Pokémon Venusaur is attacked with\nthe Water-type move Hydro Pump.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Has No Effect[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nAn attack that has no effect will deal [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]no damage[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nExample:\nWhen the Ghost-type Pokémon Gengar is attacked with\nthe Normal-type move Hyper Voice.
Pokémon with Two Types
Some Pokémon have two types instead of one.\n\nWhen a Pokémon with two types is hit by a move, the type\nmatchup for each of the Pokémon’s types will be combined\nto determine the final matchup between that Pokémon and\nthe move used on it. This can lead to the following two\nmatchups: [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]extremely effective[System:Color a="255" ] and [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]mostly ineffective[System:Color a="255" ].
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Extremely Effective[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nAn attack that is extremely effective will deal [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]four times[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]as much damage[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nExample:\nWhen the Bug- and Steel-type Pokémon Scizor is attacked\nwith the Fire-type move Flamethrower.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Mostly Ineffective[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nAn attack that is mostly ineffective will only deal [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]a quarter as[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]much damage[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nExample:\nWhen the Bug- and Steel-type Pokémon Scizor is attacked\nwith the Grass-type move Solar Beam.
Using Moves of the Same Type as Your Pokémon
When a Pokémon uses a move of the same type as one of the\nPokémon’s types, the move’s [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]damage will be increased by 50%[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nExample:\nWhen the Electric-type Pokémon Pikachu attacks with the\nElectric-type move Thunderbolt.
Notable Traits of Grass, Fire, Electric, and Flying Types
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Grass Types[System:Color a="255" ]\n\n ・ Are immune to Leech Seed\n ・ Are immune to moves and Abilities involving powder
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Fire Types[System:Color a="255" ]\n\n ・ Cannot be burned
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Electric Types[System:Color a="255" ]\n\n ・ Cannot be paralyzed
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Flying Types[System:Color a="255" ]\n\n ・ Are immune to the Spikes, Toxic Spikes, and Sticky Web\n     statuses
Notable Traits of Rock, Poison, Ground, and Ice Types
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Rock Types[System:Color a="255" ]\n\n ・ Have their Sp. Def stats boosted by 50% in sandstorms\n ・ Do not take damage from sandstorms
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Poison Types[System:Color a="255" ]\n\n ・ Cannot be poisoned or badly poisoned\n ・ Remove the Toxic Spikes status when switched into battle
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Ground Types[System:Color a="255" ]\n\n ・ Are immune to Thunder Wave\n ・ Do not take damage from sandstorms
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Ice Types[System:Color a="255" ]\n\n ・ Cannot be frozen\n ・ Have their Defense stats boosted by 50% in snow\n ・ Are immune to Sheer Cold
Notable Traits of Ghost, Dark, and Steel Types
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Ghost Types[System:Color a="255" ]\n\n ・ Are immune to the Can’t Escape status
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Dark Types[System:Color a="255" ]\n\n ・ Are immune to status moves that have their priority increased\n    by Prankster
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Steel Types[System:Color a="255" ]\n\n ・ Cannot be poisoned or badly poisoned\n ・ Do not take damage from sandstorms
Time Limits
There are a variety of different [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]time limits[System:Color a="255" ] that come into play\nwhen battling. If you don’t make a decision in time, an action\nwill automatically be decided for you to keep the battle moving.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Total Time\n[System:Color a="255" ]\nThis is the total time available for the entire battle.\n\nIf this time runs out, the battle will end, and the result will be a\ndraw if you’re having a Casual Battle or Ranked Battle.\nA draw doesn’t award Victory Points (VP) or Season Points (SP),\nand your rank does not change.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Your Time[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThis is the total time that you, as an individual, are given to\ndecide all your actions in a battle.\n\nIf you run out of this time, the battle will end, and it will be\nconsidered a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]loss[System:Color a="255" ] for you.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Move Time (Per Turn)[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThis is the time that you’re given each turn to decide\nwhat action you want to take on that particular turn.\n\nIf you don’t decide an action before this time runs out,\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]your Pokémon will automatically use whichever move is[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]at the top of their list of moves[System:Color a="255" ].
Advanced Battling Know-How
Stat Changes
A Pokémon’s stats can be boosted or lowered during a battle\nby effects from sources such as moves, Abilities, and held items.\nThis is called a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]stat change[System:Color a="255" ].
Stat changes are measured in stages ranging from [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]−6 to +6[System:Color a="255" ].\nThe negative numbers indicate that a stat has been lowered,\nwhile the positive numbers indicate that it has been boosted.\n\nWhen a Pokémon is switched out of battle, these numbers\nwill be [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]reset to zero[System:Color a="255" ].
Stat changes can affect more than just a Pokémon’s stats,\nsuch as Attack and Defense. They can also affect a\nPokémon’s [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]evasiveness[System:Color a="255" ] and [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]accuracy[System:Color a="255" ].
When your Pokémon’s evasiveness is lowered, it will have a\nharder time evading moves. When its evasiveness is boosted,\nit becomes more likely that your opponents’ moves will miss.\n\nWhen your Pokémon’s accuracy is lowered, it will have a harder\ntime hitting targets with its moves. When its accuracy is boosted,\nit is more likely to be able to hit targets with its moves.
Critical Hits
A Pokémon’s moves have a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]1-in-24 chance[System:Color a="255" ] of landing\nas a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]critical hit[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nA critical hit will boost a move’s damage by [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]50%[System:Color a="255" ].
In addition, a critical hit will [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]ignore certain stat changes and[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]status changes[System:Color a="255" ].
When a Pokémon gains a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Critical-Hit Ratio Boost[System:Color a="255" ], its odds of\nlanding a critical hit will be increased.\n\nThe Critical-Hit Ratio Boost status has stages that range from\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]0 to +3[System:Color a="255" ]. The larger the number, the more likely the Pokémon\nwill be to land a critical hit.
Status Conditions
A Pokémon can be afflicted with a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]status condition[System:Color a="255" ] during a\nbattle by the effect of a move, Ability, or held item.\n\nThese status conditions can have a variety of effects.
Check out the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]battle tutorial on status conditions [System:Color a="255" ]to learn\nmore about them through a hands-on demonstration.
The Poisoned, Badly Poisoned, and Burned Status Conditions
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Poisoned Status Condition[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThe Pokémon takes damage equal to 1/8 of its max HP\nat the end of every turn.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Badly Poisoned Status Condition[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThe Pokémon takes increasing poison damage at the end of\nevery turn, starting at 1/16 of the Pokémon’s max HP, then\n2/16, then 3/16, and so on. If the Pokémon switches out and\nreenters battle, the damage restarts at 1/16 of its max HP.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Burned Status Condition[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThe Pokémon takes damage equal to 1/16 of its max HP\nat the end of every turn. The damage dealt by its physical\nmoves is also halved.
The Paralyzed, Frozen, and Asleep Status Conditions
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Paralyzed Status Condition[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThe Pokémon has a 12.5% chance of being unable to use\nmoves. Its Speed stat is also halved.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Frozen Status Condition[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThe Pokémon can’t use almost any moves but has a 25%\nchance of being cured each time it tries to do so. The\nPokémon will be cured on its third turn after becoming\nfrozen or if it takes damage from a Fire-type move or\ncertain other moves.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Asleep Status Condition[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThe Pokémon can’t use moves other than Snore or\nSleep Talk. After a Pokémon is put to sleep, it will\nremain asleep on its first turn, it will have a 1-in-3\nchance of being cured on its second turn, and it will be\ncured on its third turn. A Pokémon that used the move\nRest has no chance of being cured until its third turn.
Battle Statuses and Effects
During battles, [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]various statuses and effects[System:Color a="255" ] can be\ncaused by moves, Abilities, and held items.\n\nLet’s look at a few examples.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Trick Room Status\n[System:Color a="255" ]\nPokémon with lower Speed stats move first.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Tailwind Status\n[System:Color a="255" ]\nDoubles the Pokémon’s Speed stat.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Reflect Status\n[System:Color a="255" ]\nHalves the damage taken from physical moves.\nIn Double Battles, this damage is reduced by\n1/3 instead.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Light Screen Status\n[System:Color a="255" ]\nHalves the damage taken from special moves.\nIn Double Battles, this damage is reduced by\n1/3 instead.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Aurora Veil Status\n[System:Color a="255" ]\nHalves the damage taken from physical and\nspecial moves. In Double Battles, this damage\nis reduced by 1/3 instead.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Stealth Rock Status[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nPokémon that switch into battle will take damage\nequal to 1/8 of their max HP. This damage differs\ndepending on the Pokémon’s type matchup with\nthe Rock type.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Spikes Status[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nPokémon that switch into battle will take damage\nequal to 1/8 of their max HP. This damage will\nincrease if 2 layers of Spikes are set, and again if\n3 layers are set. Pokémon such as Flying types or\nones with the Levitate Ability are unaffected.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Toxic Spikes Status[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nPokémon that switch into battle will be poisoned\nor, if 2 layers of Toxic Spikes are set, badly\npoisoned. Pokémon such as Flying types or ones\nwith the Levitate Ability are unaffected.
Weather Conditions
The effects of some moves and Abilities can change the\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]weather[System:Color a="255" ] during battle.\n\nWeather impacts [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]all Pokémon on the field[System:Color a="255" ] and can cause\na variety of effects.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Harsh Sunlight[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nBoosts the damage dealt by Fire-type moves by 50%\nand halves the damage dealt by Water-type moves.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Rain[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nBoosts the damage dealt by Water-type moves by 50%\nand halves the damage dealt by Fire-type moves.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Sandstorm[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nPokémon that are not Rock, Ground, or Steel types take\ndamage equal to 1/16 of their max HP at the end of every\nturn. Boosts the Sp. Def stats of Rock-type Pokémon by 50%.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Snow[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nBoosts the Defense stats of Ice-type Pokémon by 50%.
Check out the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]battle tutorial on weather conditions[System:Color a="255" ] to learn\nmore about them through a hands-on demonstration.
Terrains
The effects of some moves and Abilities can create a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]terrain[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nTerrains impact [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]all Pokémon on the ground[System:Color a="255" ] and can cause\na variety of effects.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Electric Terrain[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nPokémon on the ground have the power of their Electric-type\nmoves boosted by 30% and they cannot fall asleep.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Psychic Terrain\n[System:Color a="255" ]\nPokémon on the ground have the power of their Psychic-type\nmoves boosted by 30% and they are immune to priority moves.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Grassy Terrain[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nPokémon on the ground have the power of their Grass-type\nmoves boosted by 30% and they have 1/16 of their max HP\nrestored at the end of every turn.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Misty Terrain[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nPokémon on the ground have the power of their Dragon-type\nmoves halved, they are immune to status conditions, and they\ncannot become confused.
Check out the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]battle tutorial on terrains [System:Color a="255" ]to learn more\nabout them through a hands-on demonstration.
Move Categories
Moves can be divided into three groups: [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]physical moves[System:Color a="255" ],\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]special moves[System:Color a="255" ], and [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]status moves[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nCollectively, these are called [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]move categories[System:Color a="255" ].
The damage dealt by [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]physical moves[System:Color a="255" ] is calculated using the\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Attack stat[System:Color a="255" ] of the Pokémon using the move as well as the\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Defense stat[System:Color a="255" ] of the Pokémon hit by the move.
The damage dealt by [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]special moves[System:Color a="255" ] is calculated using the\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Sp. Atk stat[System:Color a="255" ] of the Pokémon using the move as well as the\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Sp. Def stat[System:Color a="255" ] of the Pokémon hit by the move.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Status moves[System:Color a="255" ] don’t deal damage and don’t have an associated\nmove power, but they can cause [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]a variety of other effects[System:Color a="255" ].
Check out the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]battle tutorial on physical vs. special moves[System:Color a="255" ]\nto learn more about them through a hands-on demonstration.
Priority
All moves have a numerical value that represents their [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]priority[System:Color a="255" ].\n\nMove priorities range from [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]−7 to +5[System:Color a="255" ]. Pokémon using a move\nwith higher priority will act first, regardless of their Speed stat.
If your Pokémon and the opponent’s Pokémon both use moves\nwith the same priority, the order in which they use their moves\nwill be determined by which of them has the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]higher Speed stat[System:Color a="255" ].
Check out the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]battle tutorial on move priority [System:Color a="255" ]to learn more\nabout it through a hands-on demonstration.
Range
Each move has a set [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]range[System:Color a="255" ] in which its effects take place.
A move can have one of eleven ranges: [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]single target[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]self[System:Color a="255" ],\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]single ally[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]all Pokémon[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]all allies[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]all opponents[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]random[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]opponent[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]entire field[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]opponent’s side[System:Color a="255" ], [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]user’s side[System:Color a="255" ], and [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]varies[System:Color a="255" ].
Single Target, Self, Single Ally, All Pokémon
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Single Target[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nMoves with this range will affect one Pokémon other than\nthe user.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Self[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nMoves with this range will affect only the user.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Single Ally[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nMoves with this range will affect an ally other than the user.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]All Pokémon[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nMoves with this range will usually affect every Pokémon except\nthe user. Some moves, however, will also affect the user.
All Allies, All Opponents, Random Opponent, Entire Field
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]All Allies[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nMoves with this range will affect all allies including the user.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]All Opponents[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nMoves with this range will affect all opponents.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Random Opponent[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nMoves with this range will affect one opponent at random.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Entire Field[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nMoves with this range will affect all Pokémon on the field.
Opponent’s Side, User’s Side, Varies
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Opponent’s Side[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nMoves with this range will affect the side of the field\nbelonging to all opponents.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]User’s Side[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nMoves with this range will affect the side of the field\nbelonging to the user and its allies.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Varies[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nMoves with this range will affect Pokémon in ways that are\ndifferent from the other ranges.
Check out the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]battle tutorial on Double Battles[System:Color a="255" ] to learn\nmore about them through a hands-on demonstration.
Contact
Moves can be broadly divided into two groups:\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]contact moves[System:Color a="255" ], which make contact with the target, and\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]noncontact moves[System:Color a="255" ], which don’t make contact with the target.\n\nThere are a variety of moves, held items, and Abilities that can\neither affect contact moves or are triggered by contact moves.\n\nLet’s look at some examples.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]King’s Shield[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nThe user protects itself from incoming attacks for the turn and\nchanges into its Shield Forme. Any attackers that use contact\nmoves against the user during this turn will have their Attack\nstats lowered by 1 stage. With each consecutive use, this\nmove’s chance of success becomes 1/3 of what it was before.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Rough Skin[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nWhen the Pokémon is hit by a contact move, the attacker takes\ndamage equal to 1/8 of its max HP.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Tough Claws[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nBoosts the power of the Pokémon’s contact moves by 30%.
Check out the [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]battle tutorial on contact vs. noncontact moves[System:Color a="255" ]\nto learn more about them through a hands-on demonstration.
Move Classifications
There are many moves that can be given a particular\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]classification[System:Color a="255" ], with each of those classifications containing\nmoves that share similar characteristics.\n\nLet’s look at [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]powder[System:Color a="255" ] and [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]sound-based[System:Color a="255" ] moves as examples.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Powder Moves[System:Color a="255" ]\n\n ・ Have no effect against Pokémon with the Overcoat Ability\n ・ Have no effect against Grass-type Pokémon
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Sound-Based Moves[System:Color a="255" ]\n\n ・ Have no effect against Pokémon with the Soundproof Ability\n ・ Can ignore the effects of substitutes
Other
VP
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]VP (Victory Points)[System:Color a="255" ] can be used to recruit and train Pokémon,\nobtain things in the Frontier Shop, and more.
You can obtain VP through taking part in Ranked Battles.\n\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Winning Ranked Battles will reward you with more VP[System:Color a="255" ] than\nlosing will.
You can also obtain VP via Cordy’s missions, Battle Passes, and\nthrough other means.
Tickets
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Tickets[System:Color a="255" ] are used for recruiting Pokémon, training Pokémon, and\nmore. There are various types of tickets you can obtain.\n\nLet’s look at some examples.
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Quick Coupons[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nQuick Coupons [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]shorten [System:Color a="255" ]how long you must wait to recruit a\nPokémon by [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]one hour per ticket[System:Color a="255" ].
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Teammate Tickets[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nA Teammate Ticket can be used to reduce the cost of\npermanently recruiting a Pokémon to [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]0 VP[System:Color a="255" ].
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Training Tickets[System:Color a="255" ]\n\nA Training Ticket can be used to reduce the cost of\ntraining a Pokémon to [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]0 VP[System:Color a="255" ].
Membership
If you purchase a [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]membership[System:Color a="255" ], you’ll be able\nto do the following:\n\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ] ・ Store more Pokémon in your Box[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ] ・ Have more Battle Teams usable at one time[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ] ・ Unlock membership-exclusive missions[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ] ・ Unlock membership-exclusive battle songs[System:Color a="255" ]
Your Region and Location
Your [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]region and location[System:Color a="255" ] affect which Online Competitions\nyou’re able to participate in.
Please adjust your region and location as necessary whenever\nyou change your place of residence.
Linking Accounts
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]You can use the same game data on both the Nintendo Switch[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]version and mobile version of Pokémon Champions[System:Color a="255" ] by linking\nthe same Nintendo Account to both.
Data Carryover
Linking accounts will allow you to [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]carry over your[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Pokémon Champions data[System:Color a="255" ] even if you uninstall the\napplication or change to a new mobile device or console.
If you want to carry over your data to a new device,\nsuch as when you’re changing mobile devices, [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]make[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]sure to use your current device to link accounts[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]before you do so[System:Color a="255" ].
You can carry over your Pokémon Champions data by\nopening up the Pokémon Champions app in your new\ndevice or console and then [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]logging in to the linked account[System:Color a="255" ].
Linking accounts will allow you to [System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]carry over your[System:Color a="255" ]\n[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Pokémon Champions data[System:Color a="255" ] even if you uninstall the\napplication or change to a new mobile device or console.
Competition Mode
[System:Color r="255" g="128" b="128" a="255" ]Competition Mode[System:Color a="255" ] is a special mode used during events\nsuch as Offline Competitions.\n\nYou can enter Competition Mode from the menu on the\ntitle screen.

Welcome to the world of Pokémon!
The mysterious creatures known as\nPokémon live in all sorts of places...
Both out in nature and here in our cities—\nPokémon truly are everywhere!
Pokémon love to compete with each\nother and battle alongside people.
And this is where the best come to battle:\nthe Battle Arena in the city of Frontier.
Within this arena, Pokémon Trainers face\neach other in fierce battles day and night.
Caraway\nOwner of the Battle Arena
Kajima\nMayor of Frontier
Trainers who battle their way to the top\nin the Battle Arena are known as...
Pokémon Champions!
This title is revered throughout Frontier...\nand indeed throughout the entire world!
Who will be next to claim the title\nand the crown alongside it?

You can’t change your membership plan while your current one is active.\n\nIf you would like to change to a different membership plan, please cancel\nthe automatic renewal for your current plan.\n\nThen, once your current plan has expired and your membership is no longer\nactive, you can purchase your preferred membership plan.

Restore Transactions

[~ 59]
All transactions successfully restored!
・ Product Details and Quantity\nPremium Battle Pass ×1\nPurchasing a Premium Battle Pass lets you receive additional rewards when the level of your\nBattle Pass increases.\nFor more specifics about these rewards, please check the Battle Pass screen, which can be\naccessed from the Gym screen.\n\nA Premium Battle Pass remains valid for the duration of the season.\nAfter the season ends, the pass will expire. You can purchase a new Premium Battle Pass for\nthe next season. To see the specific dates of a season, please check the Battle Pass screen,\nwhich can be accessed from the Gym screen.\n\nNote: Rewards that are identical to items you already have in your inventory may be\nconverted to VP.\n\nAt the time of purchasing a Premium Battle Pass, you’ll receive the Premium Battle Pass\nrewards for all of the Battle Pass levels that you’ve attained up until that point.\n\nNote: Rewards obtained with the Premium Battle Pass may become available to purchase\nfrom the Shop screen or to obtain in some other way at a later date.\n\n\n・ Pricing\nTo see the price of this product, please select [Character2:L_DoubleQuot. ]Back[Character2:R_DoubleQuot. ] to return to the previous screen and\ncheck the information there.\n\n\n・ Sales Period\nYou can purchase a Premium Battle Pass up until the end of the season during which that pass\nis being sold.\nOnly one Premium Battle Pass may be purchased per sales period.\n\nIf you attempt to purchase a Premium Battle Pass right before the end of the sales period, it’s\npossible that the transaction may not go through due to payment issues on the platform.\n\nPlease ensure that you have sufficient time before the end of the sales period when you\npurchase a Premium Battle Pass.\n
[~ 62]
[~ 63]
[~ 64]
[~ 65]
1. Membership Benefits (pricing and other details)\nTwo types of membership plans are available: a 1-month plan and a 12-month plan.\nTo see the prices of these products, please select [Character2:L_DoubleQuot. ]Back[Character2:R_DoubleQuot. ] to return to the previous screen and\ncheck the information there.\n\nYou can receive the following benefits by purchasing a membership, depending on the region.\n\n・ The capacity of your Box will increase by 1,000 Pokémon.\n・ The number of Battle Teams you can use will increase by 15.\n・ Membership-exclusive missions will be unlocked (applicable missions can be seen on the\n   Missions screen).\n・ Membership-exclusive battle songs will be unlocked (applicable battle songs will be\n   indicated by a gold label and can be seen on the screen for changing battle songs).\n\nYou can receive these benefits immediately after purchasing a membership.\n\nIf you cancel your membership, you will still be able to receive these benefits until your\nmembership period expires. Please note that you will not receive a refund for canceling\nyour membership.\n\n\n2. Automatic Membership Renewal\nAfter you become a member, your membership will be renewed upon the renewal date of\nyour purchased plan, and you will be charged automatically.\nNote: Please be aware that your membership period may differ depending on your method\nof purchase.\n\n------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\nMembership periods for players using the Nintendo Switch version of the game\nwith automatic renewal active:\n1-month plan: Until the same time on the 30th day after purchase.\n12-month plan: Until the same time on the 365th day after purchase (where permitted).\n\nFor example:\nIf you purchase a 1-month (30-day) plan at 3:00 p.m. on January 1, 2026, the plan will\nautomatically be renewed for 30 more days at 3:00 p.m. on January 31, 2026.\n\nIf you purchase a 12-month (365-day) plan at 5:00 a.m. on January 1, 2026, the plan will\nautomatically be renewed for 12 more months at 5:00 a.m. on January 1, 2027.\n\n\nMembership periods for players using the mobile version of the game with automatic\nrenewal active:\n1-month plan: Until 1 month after purchase (i.e. until the same time on the same day of the\nfollowing month).\n12-month plan: Until 1 year after purchase (i.e. until the same time on the same day of the\nfollowing year). (Where permitted)\nIf you purchase a membership at the end of the month, and the equivalent day does not exist\nduring the following month or year, your membership will instead be renewed at the same\ntime on the final day of the relevant month.\n\nFor example:\nIf you purchase a 1-month plan at 3:00 p.m. on January 1, 2026, the plan will\nautomatically be renewed for 1 more month at 3:00 p.m. on February 1, 2026.\n\nIf you purchase a 12-month plan at 5:00 a.m. on January 1, 2026, the plan will\nautomatically be renewed for 12 more months at 5:00 a.m. on January 1, 2027\n(where permitted).\n------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\nAs soon as your membership expires, you will stop being able to receive the benefits from\nyour membership plan.\nNote: Automatic membership renewal may not work in certain regions and locations\ndepending on the age of the player.\nNote: When playing the mobile version, please log in with a device that is compatible with\nthe platform used to purchase your membership. The automatic renewal of your membership\nmay not be reflected properly if you log in with a device that uses a different platform.\n\nIf you do not want your membership to renew automatically, please cancel the automatic\nrenewal on the platform you used to become a member:\n・ at least 48 hours before the end of the current membership period for the Nintendo Switch\n   version, and\n・ at least 24 hours before the end of the current membership period for the mobile version.\n\nFor more guidance on how to cancel automatic renewal, please check the official customer\nsupport site for Pokémon Champions.\n\n\n3. Membership Cancellation Information\nIf you cancel your membership, you will no longer be able to receive the benefits from your\nmembership plan, and certain features of the game will change as below.\n\n・ The capacity of your Box will revert to 30 slots, plus any additional slots earned by\n   other means.\n・ Any Pokémon that can no longer fit in your Box will be locked. You won’t be able to do the\n   following with locked Pokémon.\n     1) Register them to Battle Teams\n     2) Have them take part in battles\n     3) Train them\n     4) Change their battle names\n     5) Change their titles\n     6) Issue or use Team IDs for any teams they are on\n\n・ You can do the following with locked Pokémon.\n     1) Return them to Roster Ranch\n     2) Send them back to Pokémon HOME\n     3) Add them to your favorites or unfavorite them\n     4) Give them labels or remove labels from them\n\n・ Even if you return recruited Pokémon to Roster Ranch or send visiting Pokémon back\n   to Pokémon HOME, your locked Pokémon will not be unlocked to fill the newly-created\n   spaces in your Box.\n・ Pokémon that were permanently recruited in Pokémon Champions and that are currently\n   eligible to take part in Ranked Battles will be the last in line to be locked.\n・ Locked Pokémon will be unlocked as soon as you purchase a membership again.\n\n・ The number of Battle Teams you can use will decrease by 15.\n\n・ You will no longer be able to receive rewards from membership-exclusive missions\n   (applicable missions can be seen on the Missions screen).\n\n・ You will no longer be able to select membership-exclusive battle songs (applicable\n   battle songs will be indicated by a gold label and can be seen on the screen for\n   changing battle songs).\n\n\n4. Platform Used to Enroll in Membership\nIf you are using the same account to play the Nintendo Switch version and the mobile version\nof Pokémon Champions, you can enroll in membership from either version but not both at the\nsame time.\nYou can claim membership benefits regardless of which version of the game you used to\nbecome a member, whether it is the Nintendo Switch version or the mobile version.\n\n\n5. Other Information\n・ If you reinstall the app due to a change of device or other reason, please link your game to\n   the relevant account and log in with the account you want to have associated with your\n   membership before you purchase the membership.\n・ Payment issues on the platform may cause errors in processing your membership enrollment.\n   Please do not close the app while payments are being processed.\n・ If you are playing the mobile version of Pokémon Champions and you are not able to claim\n   your membership benefits despite having purchased a membership, please try selecting the\n   following options, starting from the Gym screen.\n   Shop > Premium Shop > Membership > Restore Past Transactions\n
